The Usuli Distinction Between Ada (Performance) and Qada (Making Up)
Explaining the usul definition of ada and qada and the argument for qada via qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada and qada, identify the two types of ada (pure and deficient), and explain why qada for a missed vow is based on qiyas on the original cause.

Core Idea
Ada is performing worship as prescribed; qada is making up by qiyas on the original cause.

This lesson unpacks the usul distinction between performance and making up. The author clarifies that ada can be pure or deficient, and qada is linked by qiyas to the original obligation, not directly to the vow. Understanding this distinction is key to applying rules for missed acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Define ada and its categories
Identify the passage's definition: ada is performing worship in its time (mu'aqqata) or any time (ghayr mu'aqqata). Note the two types: mahd (pure, e.g., congregational prayer) and qasir (deficient, e.g., individual prayer).
The term mahd means 'pure' or 'perfect'.
2
Define qada and its basis
Qada is making up after the time. The passage argues qada is linked to the original cause by qiyas, not directly from a vow.
The original cause for missed Ramadan fasts is expiry (fawat); for vows, it is loss (tafweed).
3
Analyze the dispute over vowed acts
Some opponents claim qada for a missed vow is due to loss itself, making it like an absolute vow. The Hanafi response: qada is by qiyas on the original cause, not by text on the vow.
Hanafi position: qada is obligatory by qiyas.
4
Distinguish pure ada from deficient ada
Pure ada is performing exactly as prescribed (e.g., prayer in congregation). Deficient ada lacks some elements (e.g., loud recitation dropped for individual).
Individual prayer is still ada, but deficient.
5
Apply the distinction to a modern scenario
Consider a person who vowed to fast on the 15th of Sha'ban but missed it. According to Hanafi usul, qada is required by qiyas on missed Ramadan fasts.
The vow creates an obligation, and missing it triggers qada via tafweed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : لأن القضاء إنما وجب ابتداء بالتفويت لا بالنذر، والتفويت سبب مطلق عن الوقت، فصار كالنذر المطلق عن الوقت. لكنا نقول إنما وجب القضاء في هذا بالقياس على ما قلنا لا بنص مقصود في هذا الباب، وإذا ثبت هذا لم يكن بد من إضافته إلى السبب الأول. ألا يُرى أنه يجب بالفوات مرةً، وبالتفويت أخرى، إلا أن الاعتكاف الواجب بالنذر مطلقاً يقتضي صوماً، للاعتكاف أثر في إيجابه. وإنما جاء هذا النقصان في مسألة شهر رمضان بعارض شَرَفِ الوقت، وما ثبت بشرف الوقت فقد فات بحيث لا يتمكن من اكتساب مثله إلا : بالحياة إلى رمضان آخر، وهو وقت مديد تستوي فيه الحياة والموت، فلم تثبت القدرة، فسقط، فبقي مضموناً بإطلاقه. وكان هذا أحوط الوجهين ؛ لأن ما ثبت بشرف الوقت من الزيادة لما احتمل السقوط، فالنقصان والرخصة الواقعة بالشرف لأنْ يَحتمل السقوط والعود إلى الكمال أولى، فإذا عاد لم يتأدَّ في الرمضان الثاني، والأداء في العبادات يكون في المؤقتة في الوقت وفي غير المؤقتة أبداً، على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى. والمحض منه : ما يؤديه الإنسان بوصفه على ما شرع له، مثل أداء الصلاة بجماعة، وأما فعل المنفرد فأداء فيه قصور، ألا يُرى أن الجهر عن المنفرد ساقط، والشارع مع الإمام في الجماعة مؤد أداء محضاً. والمسبوق ببعض الصلاة مؤدِّ أيضاً ، لكنه منفرد ، فكان قاصراً. ومَن نام خلف الإمام ، أو أحدث، فذهب يتوضأ، ثم عاد بعد فراغ الإمام من الصلاة: فهذا مؤدَّ أداءً يُشبه القضاء، ألا يُرى أنهم قالوا في مسافر اقتدى بمسافر في الوقت ثم سبقه ،الحدث، أو نام حتى فرغ الإمام من صلاته، ثم سبقه الحدث، فدخل مصره للوضوء، أو نوى الإقامة وهو في غير مصره والوقت باق: فإنه يصلي ركعتين، ولو تكلم صلى أربعاً. ولو كان الإمام بعد لم يفرغ ، أو كان هذا الرجل مسبوقاً: صلى أربعاً، ولو تكلم : صلى أربعاً، كما في المسألة الأُولى. وأصل ذلك : أن هذا مؤدَّ باعتبار الوقت، لكنه قاض باعتبار فراغ الإمام؛ لأنه كأنه خلف الإمام حُكماً، لا أنه في الحقيقة خلفه، فصار قاضياً لما انعقد له إحرام الإمام بمثله. والمثل بطريق القضاء إنما يجب بالسبب الذي أوجب الأصل، فما لم يتغير الأصل: لا يتغير المثل. فإذا لم يفرغ الإمام حتى وُجد من المقتدي ما يوجب إكمال صلاته : تمت صلاته بنية إقامته، أو بدخول مصره ؛ لأنه مؤدِّ في الوقت. فأما إذا فرغ الإمام، ثم وُجد ما ذكرنا فإنما اعترض هذا على القضاء، دون الأداء، فإذا لم يتغير الأداء : لم يتغير القضاء، كما إذا صار قضاء محضاً بالفوات عن الوقت، ثم وُجد المغير، وإذا تكلم: فقد بطل معنى القضاء، وعاد الأمر إلى الأداء، فتغير بالمغير؛ لقيام الوقت. بخلاف المسبوق أيضاً؛ لأنه مؤدِّ ، ولهذا قلنا في اللاحق إنه لا يقرأ، ولا يسجد للسهو، بخلاف المسبوق ؛ لما بينا أنه قاض لما انعقد له إحرام الجماعة. وأما القضاء فنوعان : إما بمثل معقول، كما ذكرنا
They said: Because qada (making up) was initially made obligatory by the loss (tafweed) [of the act] and not by the vow (nadhr). And loss is an absolute cause unrelated to time, so it becomes like an absolute vow unrelated to time. But we say: Qada in this is only made obligatory by analogy (qiyas) on what we said, not by a specific text in this chapter. And once this is established, it must be attributed to the first cause. Do you not see that it is obligatory once by expiry (fawat) and another time by loss (tafweed)? However, the i'tikaf (retreat) made obligatory by a vow absolutely necessitates fasting, because i'tikaf has an effect in making it obligatory. And this deficiency only came in the case of the month of Ramadan due to the incidental honor of the time (sharaf al-waqt). And what is established by the honor of time becomes lost in such a way that one cannot acquire its like except by living until another Ramadan. And it is a long time during which life and death are equal, so ability is not established, and it falls away, so it remains guaranteed [as an obligation] absolutely. And this was the more cautious of the two ways; because when what is established by the honor of time, in terms of increase, is susceptible to falling away, then the decrease and concession occurring due to honor are even more likely to fall away and return to the complete [obligation]. So when it returns, it is not fulfilled in the second Ramadan. And performance (ada) in acts of worship is in time-bound [acts] within the time, and in non-time-bound [acts] always, as we will explain, God willing. And the pure (mahd) [performance] is what a person performs in the manner prescribed, like performing prayer in congregation. As for the individual's act, it is a performance with deficiency. Do you not see that recitation aloud is dropped for the individual, while the one performing with the imam in congregation is a pure performer. And the one who is overtaken (masbuq) by part of the prayer is also a performer, but he is individual, so he is deficient. And one who sleeps behind the imam, or has an event (hadath), and goes to perform ablution, then returns after the imam has finished the prayer: this is a performance resembling qada. Do you not see that they said concerning a traveler who followed another traveler in time, then an event preceded him, or he slept until the imam finished his prayer, then an event preceded him, and he entered his town for ablution, or he intended residence while he was not in his town and the time remained: he prays two rak'ats, and if he speaks he prays four. And if the imam had not yet finished, or this man was overtaken (masbuq): he prays four, and if he speaks he prays four, as in the first case. The principle is that this person is a performer (mu'addin) in consideration of the time, but he is making up (qadin) in consideration of the imam's completion; because he is as if behind the imam in legal fiction (hukman), not in reality, so he becomes a maker-up for what the imam's ihram was contracted for by its like. And the like by way of qada is only obligatory by the cause that made the original obligatory; so as long as the original does not change, the like does not change. If the imam has not finished until something occurs from the follower that necessitates completing his prayer: his prayer is completed by his intention of residence or by entering his town, because he is a performer in time. But if the imam has finished, then what we mentioned occurs, then this affects the qada, not the performance; so if performance does not change, qada does not change, as when it becomes pure qada by the expiry of time, then a changer occurs. And if he speaks, then the meaning of qada is invalidated and the matter returns to performance, so it changes by the changer because the time remains. Unlike the overtaken (masbuq) as well, because he is a performer; for this reason we say about the one who joins later (lahiq) that he does not recite and does not perform prostration of forgetfulness, unlike the masbuq, because we have clarified that he is making up for what the congregation's ihram was contracted for. As for qada, it is of two types: either by a rational like (mithl ma'qul), as we mentioned.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul analysis of the distinction between ada (performance) and qada (making up) in acts of worship. The author begins by addressing an objection: opponents (possibly early Hanafis or others) argued that qada for a missed vow obligation is due to the loss of the act itself (tafweed), not the vow, making it analogous to an absolute vow. The author responds that the obligation of qada is established by qiyas (analogy) on the principle that qada is linked to the original cause, not by a specific text. In the case of Ramadan, a deficiency (not fasting the missed day) occurs due to the honor of the time (sharaf al-waqt) – the missed fast cannot be made up until the next Ramadan, a period where life and death are uncertain, so the obligation is maintained absolutely.

The passage then defines ada and qada more precisely. Ada is performing the act in its proper time (for time-bound acts) or at any time (for non-time-bound acts). Pure (mahd) ada is performing exactly as prescribed, e.g., congregational prayer. Individual prayer is ada but deficient (qasir) because elements like loud recitation are dropped. A person who sleeps or has a hadath behind the imam and returns after the imam finishes is performing an ada that resembles qada (shabih bi al-qada).

The text then examines a specific case: a traveller following a traveller imam. If an event occurs before the imam finishes, the follower's prayer is completed according to his new status (e.g., if he intends residence, he prays full). If the imam has finished before the event, the follower's prayer becomes qada, and changes in his status (like entering his town) do not affect it. If he speaks, the qada aspect is invalidated and he must perform the full prayer because time remains.

Finally, the author distinguishes between masbuq (one who misses part of the prayer with the imam) and lahiq (one who joins late). The masbuq is performing (mu'addi) and thus recites and does sajdah sahw in his own part; the lahiq is considered making up (qadi) for what he missed, so he does not recite nor perform sajdah sahw. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh. The passage concludes by stating that qada is of two types: one based on a rational like (mithl ma'qul), as discussed.

Key Terms
أداء (Adā’): Performing an act of worship in its proper time (for time-bound acts) or at any time (for non-time-bound acts).
قضاء (Qaḍā’): Making up an act of worship after its prescribed time has passed, due to the original cause of obligation.
مسبوق (Masbūq): One who joins the congregation late and misses one or more rak'ats of the prayer with the imam.
لاحق (Lāḥiq): One who joins the imam after the prayer has started but before it ends, missing some part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the defining characteristic of pure (mahd) ada?
A) Performing an act in its proper time.
B) Performing an act exactly as prescribed, e.g., prayer in congregation.
C) Performing an act alone.
D) Performing an act after its time.

Key Takeaway
Ada is performing worship as prescribed; qada is making up by qiyas on the original cause.

Applying Ada and Qada to Congregational Prayer: Masbuq and Lahiq
Applying the ada/qada distinction to masbuq and lahiq in congregational prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between a masbuq and a lahiq in terms of ada and qada, and state the rulings for their recitation and sajdah sahw.

Core Idea
A masbuq is a performer (mu'addi) and must recite; a lahiq is a maker-up (qadi) and does not recite.

This lesson applies the ada/qada distinction to specific prayer scenarios. The author explains how a person who misses part of the prayer with the imam is considered a performer (masbuq), while a person who joins late and misses some rak'ats is considered a maker-up (lahiq). This determines whether they recite and perform sajdah sahw.

Guided Path
1
Define masbuq and lahiq
A masbuq misses a rak'at or more with the imam; a lahiq joins late but catches the prayer start.
The passage gives specific rulings for each.
2
Identify the ruling for masbuq
The masbuq is a performer (mu'addi) for the part caught with the imam; he must recite and perform sajdah sahw in his own part.
He is deficient (qasir) because he is individual.
3
Identify the ruling for lahiq
The lahiq is a maker-up (qadi) for the missed part; he does not recite nor perform sajdah sahw.
The passage says: 'للاحق إنه لا يقرأ، ولا يسجد للسهو'.
4
Apply to the traveler scenario
If a traveler follows a traveler imam and has an event, his prayer status depends on whether the imam has finished.
Details: if imam finished, he is qadi; if not, he is mu'addi in time.

Source Text

قالوا : لأن القضاء إنما وجب ابتداء بالتفويت لا بالنذر، والتفويت سبب مطلق عن الوقت، فصار كالنذر المطلق عن الوقت. لكنا نقول إنما وجب القضاء في هذا بالقياس على ما قلنا لا بنص مقصود في هذا الباب، وإذا ثبت هذا لم يكن بد من إضافته إلى السبب الأول. ألا يُرى أنه يجب بالفوات مرةً، وبالتفويت أخرى، إلا أن الاعتكاف الواجب بالنذر مطلقاً يقتضي صوماً، للاعتكاف أثر في إيجابه. وإنما جاء هذا النقصان في مسألة شهر أداء (Adā’): Performing an act of worship in its proper time (for time-bound acts) or at any time (for non-time-bound acts).

According to the passage, why does a lahiq not perform sajdah sahw?
A) Because he is a performer and sajdah sahw is not required for performers.
B) Because he is making up (qadi) and the original (the part he missed) does not have sajdah sahw.
C) Because he is a traveler.

Benefits Are Not Guaranteed in Tort: The Hanafi Usul Derivation
Derivation of the ruling that benefits are not compensable in tort.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that benefits (manafi‘) are not compensable in tort and explain the derivation using the concepts of ‘arad (accident) and taqawwum (valuation).

Core Idea
Benefits are accidents that cannot be possessed, so they lack valuation and are not guaranteed in tort.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul explores why usufructs (manafi‘) are not compensable when destroyed through transgression (ta‘addi), even though they are guaranteed in contracts. The key lies in the nature of benefits as accidents (a‘raḍ) that do not persist and cannot be possessed, thus lacking the attribute of valuable property (taqawwum) required for tort liability. We'll trace the Hanafi istinbat chain that leads to this ruling and see how it differs from the Shafi‘i position.

Guided Path
1
Define the key terms
Identify and define al-manāfi‘, al-a‘rāḍ, and al-taqawwum as used in the passage. Understand that benefits are accidents that do not last for two moments and that valuation requires possession and persistence.
2
Trace the Hanafi istinbāṭ chain
Follow the four steps: (1) taḥqīq al-manāṭ establishing that manāfi‘ are a‘rāḍ; (2) taḥqīq al-manāṭ that taqawwum requires possession; (3) takhṣīṣ (exception) for contracts due to mutual consent and need; (4) invalidation of qiyās between tort and contract due to gross disparity.
3
Identify the Quranic proofs
Analyze how verses 4:24 (seeking with wealth) and 28:27 (hiring) are used. The first shows that marriage requires valuable property, implying benefits are not inherently valuable; the second shows that benefits can be contracted only as a concession.
4
Compare with the Shāfi‘ī reading
Note how the Shāfi‘ī school classifies the permissibility of contracting benefits as general evidence that benefits are valuable property, leading to a different ruling in tort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا لا تُضَمَّن منافع الأعيان بالإتلاف بطريق التعدي؛ لأن العين ليس بمثل لها لا صورة ولا معنى، أما الصورة: فلا شك فيها، وأما المعنى: فلأن المنافع إذا وجدت كانت أعراضاً لا تبقى زمانَيْن وليس لما لا يبقى زمانين صفة التقوم بحال؛ لأن التقوم لا يسبق الوجود، وبعد الوجود التقومُ لا يسبق الإحراز والاقتناء، كالصيد والحشيش والماء. والأعراض لا تقبل هذه الأوصاف إلا أن يثبت إحرازها بولاية العقد حكماً شرعياً، بناءً على جواز العقد، فلا يثبت في غير موضع العقد، بل يثبت التقوم في حكم العقد خاصة. ولأن التقوم في حكم العقد يثبت لقيام العين مقامها، وهذا أصح، ألا يُرى أن ضمان العقد ـ فاسداً كان أو جائزاً ـ يجب بالتراضي، فوجب بناء التقوم على التراضي، وضمان العدوان يعتمد أوصاف العين، والرجوع إليها يمنع التقوم على ما عُرف. ولأن التفاوت بين ما يبقى ويقومُ العَرْضُ به، وبين العرض القائم به : تفاوت فاحش، فلا يصلح مثلاً له معنى بحكم الشرع في العدوان، بخلاف ضمان العقود؛ لأن العقود مشروعة، فبنيت على الوسع والتراضي باعتبار الحاجة إليها وسقط اعتبار هذا التفاوت. ألا يُرى أن اعتبار هذا التفاوت في باب ضمان العقود يُبطلها أصلاً، واعتباره في ضمان العدوان لا يُبطله أصلاً، بل يؤخره إلى دار الجزاء؛ لأنه بطل حكماً؛ لعَجْزنا به، لا لعَدَمه في نفسه. وإهدار التفاوت يوجب ضرراً لازماً للغاصب في الدنيا والآخرة، ولم يجب التمييز بين الجائز والفاسد؛ لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى الحرج، فلم يُعتبر فيما شُرع ضرورة. والمنافع إذا وجدت لم تحتمل البقاء للإحراز، فلا تثبت لها صفة التقوم بحال. وأما جواز العقد: فبناء على قيام العين مقامَ المنفعة بطريق الخلافة؛ قضاء للحوائج، وذلك أمر مشروع عند الحاجة بالإجماع. ولا يلزم أنها تقومت في باب العقود، وليس إلى التقوم حاجة، إذ الاستبدال صحيح من غير التقوم؛ لأن ذلك ثابت بالإجماع، بخلاف القياس عند التراضي بما قلنا إن التقوم من غير إحراز غير معقول. وإنما قلنا ذلك؛ لأن الله تعالى شرع ابتغاء الأبضاع بشرط المال المتقوم، حيث قال: ﴿أَن تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُم﴾ [النساء/٢٤]، وإنما يُضاف إلينا بواسطة الإحراز. وشَرَعَ الابتغاء بالمنافع؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَى أَن تَأْجُرَنِي ثَمَانِيَ حِجَجٍ﴾ [القصص/٢٧]. وبطلت المقايسة؛ لأن للرضا أثراً في إيجاب الأصول والفضول جميعاً.
Because of this, the benefits of corporeal property are not guaranteed by way of destruction through transgression, because the corporeal property has no equivalent for them, neither in form nor in meaning. As for form, there is no doubt in it; and as for meaning: because benefits, when they come into existence, are accidents that do not persist for two moments, and that which does not persist for two moments does not have the attribute of valuation at all, because valuation does not precede existence, and after existence, valuation does not precede taking into possession and acquisition, like game, grass, and water. And accidents do not accept these attributes unless their possession is established through the authority of a contract as a legal ruling, based on the permissibility of the contract; thus it is not established outside the context of the contract; rather, valuation is established specifically in the ruling of the contract. And because valuation in the ruling of the contract is established because the corporeal property stands in their place, and this is more correct. Do you not see that the guarantee of the contract—whether invalid or permissible—is obligated by mutual consent, so valuation must be built upon mutual consent, whereas the guarantee of transgression relies on the attributes of the corporeal property, and referring to them prevents valuation as is known. And because the disparity between what persists and that by which the accident is valued, and between the accident itself that persists, is a gross disparity; so it is not suitable as an equivalent for it meaningfully by the law in transgression, unlike the guarantee of contracts, because contracts are legislated, so they are built on ease and mutual consent due to the need for them, and consideration of this disparity drops. Do you not see that considering this disparity in the context of guarantees of contracts would nullify them entirely, and considering it in the guarantee of transgression does not nullify it entirely, but rather postpones it to the Abode of Recompense; because it is nullified in legal effect due to our incapacity with it, not due to its non-existence in itself. And ignoring the disparity would entail lasting harm for the usurper in this world and the Hereafter, and it is not required to distinguish between the permissible and the invalid, because that leads to hardship, so it is not considered in what is legislated out of necessity. And benefits, when they come into existence, do not admit of persistence for possession, so the attribute of valuation is not established for them under any circumstance. As for the permissibility of the contract: it is based on the corporeal property standing in the place of the benefit by way of substitution, to fulfill needs, and this is a legislated matter when there is need by consensus. And it does not follow that they are valued in the chapter of contracts; there is no need for valuation, since substitution is valid without valuation, because that is established by consensus, unlike analogy when there is mutual consent, because we have said that valuation without possession is unintelligible. And we only said that because Allah the Exalted legislated the seeking of sexual intercourse with the condition of valuable property, where He said: "that you seek with your wealth" [4:24], and it is only attributed to us through possession. And He legislated the seeking with benefits by His saying: "on that you hire me for eight years" [28:27]. And the analogy is invalidated because consent has an effect in obligating both the essentials and the excesses all together.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and its proof. It deals with the topic of dhaman (guarantee/liability) for manafi' (usufructs/benefits) of owned objects. The ruling is that benefits are not compensable when destroyed through ta'addi (transgression/tort), unlike in contracts. The reasoning: benefits are a'rad (accidents) that do not persist for two moments, thus they cannot be possessed (ihraz) or valued (taqawwum) in the normal sense. Valuation requires existence, persistence, and possession. Benefits exist only momentarily and cannot be possessed independently. Therefore, they lack the attribute of being valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) that would make them subject to liability in tort. However, in the context of contracts, benefits are considered guaranteed because contracts are built on mutual consent and need; the law makes an exception by allowing the object itself to stand in for the benefit by way of substitution (khilafa). This is a concession (rukhsa) due to necessity, and it is established by consensus. The author also distinguishes between dhaman al-uqud (contractual liability) and dhaman al-udwan (tort liability): the former is based on mutual consent, while the latter depends on the attributes of the object itself. A key point is that if we required full valuation in contracts, contracts would be nullified; but in tort, ignoring the disparity would cause undue hardship on the usurper. The author supports the ruling with Quranic verses: 4:24 shows that marriage requires valuable property, and 28:27 shows that hiring (which involves benefits) is permissible, indicating that benefits are considered in contracts due to need, not inherent valuation. Finally, the analogy (qiyas) between tort and contract is invalidated because consent plays a crucial role in contracts.

Key Terms
المنافع (al-manāfi‘): المنافع: هي الأعيان التي توجد من استعمال العين كالسكنى والركوب، وهي أعراض لا تبقى زمانين.
الأعراض (al-a‘rāḍ): الأعراض: هي ما لا يبقى زمانين كالحركة والسكون، وتشمل المنافع.
التقوم (al-taqawwum): التقوم: صفة كون الشيء مالاً متقوماً يُضمن بإتلافه ويُعاوض عليه.
ضمان العدوان (ḍamān al-‘udwān): ضمان العدوان: هو الضمان الواجب بسبب التعدي كالغصب والإتلاف.

A) Because they are not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because they are accidents that do not persist and cannot be possessed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi Usul, benefits (manāfi‘) are non-persistent accidents and thus not valuable property in tort; their guarantee in contracts is a concession (rukhṣa) based on need and mutual consent.

Absolute Command and the Jumu'ah-Zuhr Dispute
Dispute on whether the command for Jumu'ah abrogates Zuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that an absolute command implies optimal goodness without abrogating prior obligations, and evaluate the ikhtilaf regarding Jumu'ah and Zuhr.

Core Idea
An absolute command implies the best instance of the act, but does not abrogate the original obligation—only substitutes it.

This passage examines a key usul al-fiqh debate: when Allah issues an absolute command, does it necessarily abrogate any previous similar obligation? The command for Jumu'ah prayer at Friday noon provides the test case. Shafi'i and Zufar argue that the command indicates Jumu'ah is the exclusive prescribed act, making Zuhr invalid before Jumu'ah is missed. The Hanafi school counters that the command does not abrogate Zuhr; rather, it is a substitute. As we trace the arguments, watch for the evidential weight of the qada' practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the absolute command principle
The passage opens with the claim that an absolute command requires the attribute of perfection (sifat al-hasan) in the commanded act. This means the command picks the best possible instance. Recognize that this principle underlies the entire discussion.
The 'first type of the first division' refers to acts that are good in themselves and prescribed by the command.
2
Identify the Shafi'i/Zufar position
They hold that the absolute command for Jumu'ah at zawal indicates Jumu'ah is prescribed to the exclusion of Zuhr for residents. Therefore, a resident who prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah has performed an invalid prayer.
For the excused (sick, slave, traveler), they agree Zuhr remains valid because they are not addressed by the Jumu'ah command.
3
Examine the Hanafi response and its evidence
Hanafis argue that the command does not abrogate Zuhr; it is a substitute (badal). The key evidence: after Jumu'ah is missed, Zuhr is prayed as qada' by consensus. Zuhr cannot be qada' for Jumu'ah, and Jumu'ah is not performed as qada'. This proves Zuhr remains the original obligation.
The Arabic text states: 'ألا يُرى أنه بعد فوات الجمعة: يُقضى الظهر' — 'Do you not see that after Jumu'ah is missed, Zuhr is prayed as qada'?'
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference is whether a resident who prays Zuhr on Friday before Jumu'ah has performed a valid prayer. Shafi'is rule it invalid; Hanafis hold it valid (though makruh tanzihan). The ruling affects daily practice and fatwa.
Hanafis view the prayer as valid because the obligation to pray Zuhr is not erased; Jumu'ah is simply the substitute at that time.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) because the qada' evidence is strong and based on established practice. The opposing view relies solely on the apparent meaning of the command, which is overridden by this evidence.
The text concludes that the command for Jumu'ah is a ta'yin (determination) for the time, not naskh (abrogation).

وكذلك كونه عبادة: يقتضي هذا المعنى.
ويحتمل الضرب الثاني بدليل.

وقلنا نحن لا خلاف في هذا الأصل، لكن الشأن في معرفة كيفية الأمر بالجمعة، وليس ذلك على نسخ الظهر كما قلتم.

وإنما وضع عن المعذور أداء الظهر بالجمعة؛ رخصةً، فلم تبطل العزيمة به.
وإنما قلنا إن الضرب الثالث من هذا القسم مختص بالأداء، دون
And the absolute command, in requiring the attribute of goodness, encompasses the first type of the first division; because the perfection of the command requires the perfection of the attribute of the commanded thing.
Similarly, it being worship requires this meaning.
And it [the command] may encompass the second type [only] by a proof.
And upon this is the statement of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), and it is the statement of Zufar: when the command after zawal on Friday addressed Jumu'ah, it indicated the attribute of its goodness in itself, and that it is the prescribed [act] to the exclusion of others, such that they both said: The performance of Zuhr by a resident is not valid as long as Jumu'ah has not been missed.
And they said: Since the sick, the slave, and the traveler are not addressed by Jumu'ah but rather by Zuhr, Zuhr became good and prescribed for them, so if they perform it, it is not invalidated by Jumu'ah afterward.
And we [Hanafis] said: There is no disagreement on this principle, but the issue is in knowing the nature of the command for Jumu'ah, and it is not an abrogation of Zuhr as you claim.
Do you not see that after Jumu'ah is missed, Zuhr is prayed as qada', and Zuhr is not suitable to be qada' for Jumu'ah, nor is Jumu'ah prayed as qada' by consensus. Thus it is established that it is a return to the original, and it is established that the implication of the command is performing Zuhr along with Jumu'ah [or: by means of Jumu'ah], so that became settled, not abrogating.
And indeed, the performance of Zuhr along with Jumu'ah [or: by means of Jumu'ah] was removed for the excused person as a concession, so the determination was not invalidated by it.
And we only said that the third type of this division is specific to performance, without
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of an absolute command (al-amr al-mutlaq) from Allah and what it implies regarding the goodness (husn) of the commanded act. The author categorizes three types or divisions: (1) an act that is good in itself and prescribed by the command; (2) an act that is good but only becomes prescribed by a separate proof; (3) an act specific to performance (ada') independent of original obligation.

The absolute command requires the attribute of perfection in the commanded act; therefore it selects the best possible instance. If there is another act equally good, the command might apply to it but only if evidence supports it.

A dispute is presented with al-Shafi'i and Zufar regarding the command for Jumu'ah prayer at zawal on Friday. They hold that the command indicates that Jumu'ah is the prescribed act in itself, to the exclusion of Zuhr for residents. Thus, if a resident prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah, it is invalid (unless Jumu'ah is missed). However, for those excused (sick, slave, traveler) who are addressed with Zuhr, Zuhr becomes good and prescribed for them, and once performed, it is not invalidated by later Jumu'ah.

The Hanafi response: There is agreement on the principle but disagreement on the nature of the command for Jumu'ah. It does not abrogate Zuhr; rather, the command requires performing Zuhr by means of Jumu'ah (i.e., Jumu'ah is a substitute for Zuhr at that time). Evidence: if Jumu'ah is missed, one prays Zuhr as qada', showing that Zuhr remains the original. Zuhr cannot be qada' for Jumu'ah, nor is Jumu'ah performed as qada', by consensus. Thus the command does not abrogate Zuhr but makes Jumu'ah a determined obligation for residents. The excuse of those not liable for Jumu'ah is a concession, not an abrogation.

The passage ends by stating that the third type of this division is specific to performance (ada'), without completing the thought.

Key Terms
الأمر المطلق (al-amr al-mutlaq): An unconditional command that does not specify a particular instance but requires the best possible instance of the commanded act.
صفة الحسن (sifat al-hasan): The attribute of goodness or excellence of an act, which the absolute command requires in the highest degree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, what proves that the command for Jumu'ah does not abrogate Zuhr?
A) The command for Jumu'ah is only for a specific time.
B) After Jumu'ah is missed, Zuhr is prayed as qada', showing it remains the original.
C) The sick, slave, and traveler are exempt from Jumu'ah.
D) The companions agreed that Jumu'ah is not a replacement.

Key Takeaway
The absolute command for Jumu'ah does not abrogate Zuhr; rather, it is a substitute, as evidenced by the qada' practice.

Deriving the Condition of Wealth (Yusr) for Different Obligations
Comparing obligations by purpose (ighna' vs. non-ighna')

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the varying conditions of wealth (yusr) for zakah, kaffarah, 'ushr, and kharaj by applying the Hanafi usul principle of purpose (ma'na) and analyzing the role of ighna'.

Core Idea
The purpose of an obligation determines its condition: enrichment (ighna') requires surplus wealth; expiation requires only ability.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul demonstrates the Hanafi method of istinbat by comparing four obligations. The key insight is that the underlying purpose ('illa) of each obligation dictates the level of wealth required. Zakah and sadaqat al-fitr aim to enrich the poor (ighna'), so they demand surplus wealth (ghina). Kaffarah aims to cover sin or deter, so only easy ability (yusr) is needed. Land taxes ('ushr and kharaj) are tied to the produce itself, so they are cancelled upon destruction. We will trace this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligations and their purposes
List the four obligations discussed: zakah/sadaqat al-fitr, kaffarah, 'ushr, and kharaj. For each, the author identifies a purpose: ighna' (enrichment) for the first, non-ighna' for the second, and preservation of ease for the last two.
Purpose is central to the derivation.
2
Analyze the hadith evidence for ighna'
The hadith 'Aghnuhum...' and 'La sadaqata illa an zahri ghana' establish that zakah/sadaqat al-fitr are acts of gratitude for wealth, requiring perfection in its cause. Examine how these texts are used to define the condition of ghina.
Both hadith are zanni al-thubut but give a clear meaning.
3
Understand the role of debt
The author argues that debt removes perfection (kamal) of ghina but not its origin (asl). Therefore, a person with debt may receive sadaqah but is not obliged to give it. This distinguishes sadaqat al-fitr from zakah where debt also exempts? Actually the text says debt cancels perfection, so for zakah also? The passage indicates that for zakah, debt also affects: 'din yusqitu al-kamal' and then 'la yajibu al-ighna' ' – meaning enrichment is not obligatory on the indebted. But the author says 'wa la hadha hallat lahu al-sadaqa' – so the indebted can take sadaqah. For kaffarah, debt does not negate ability because ighna' is not required.
Debt only negates the perfection of ghina, not the origin of ability.
4
Compare with kaffarah
Kaffarah is legislated as a cover (satira) or deterrent (zajira), not for ighna'. It can be fulfilled by freeing a slave or fasting – actions without enrichment. Therefore only ability (qudra) and ease (yusr) are conditions, not full ghina. Debt does not cancel ability.
The contrast is based on the purpose; kaffarah is a penalty, not a charitable act.
5
Extend to land taxes ('ushr and kharaj)
These are conditioned on easy ability (al-qudra al-muyassara) tied to the existence of produce. If produce is destroyed by a blight, the obligation is cancelled because the condition of ease is no longer met. The author uses qiyas on the same principle: the obligation depends on the attribute of ease.
The cancellation prevents the tax from becoming pure liability.

وقال بعضهم : بل تجب بالمال ولا يجزئه الصوم، بخلاف الزكاة. والفرق أن الزكاة وجبت بصفة اليُسر، وشَرْط القدرة، ولمعنى الإغناء بقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أغنوهم عن المسألة في مثل هذا اليوم). وبقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى (۲). وهذا الإغناء وجب عبادةً؛ شكراً لنعمة الغنى، فشرط الكمال في سببه ؛ ليُستحق شكره ، فيكون الواجب شطراً من الكامل، والدين يُسقط الكمال، ولا يُعدِمُ أصله. ولهذا حَلَّت له الصدقة، فلم يجب عليه الإغناء. ولهذا لا تتأدى الزكاة إلا بعين متقومة. حديث : أغنوهم عن المسألة في مثل هذا اليوم: أخرجه محمد في «الأصل» ثنا أبو معشر عن نافع عن ابن عمر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كان يأمرهم أن يؤدوا صدقة الفطر قبل أن يخرجوا إلى المصلى، وقال: أغنوهم عن المسألة في مثل هذا اليوم». وأخرجه الحاكم في علوم الحديث من هذا الوجه بلفظ : «أغنوهم عن الطواف في هذا اليوم»، ومن جهته ذكره المخرجون لأحاديث «الهداية»، والواقع في علمائنا هو اللفظ الأول. حديث : لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى: أخرجه الإمام أحمد في مسنده ثنا يعلى ابن عبيد ثنا عبد الملك عطاء عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال: قال رسول الله عن صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى، واليد العليا خير من اليد السفلى، وابدأ بمن تعول، وذكره البخاري في صحيحه تعليقاً مقتصراً على الجملة الأولى، فقال : وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى»، وتعليقاته المجزومة: لها حكم الصحة، ورواه مسنداً بغير هذا اللفظ. وأما الكفارة فلا تستغني عن شرط ،القدرة وعن قيام صفة اليسر في تلك القدرة، إلا أنها لم تُشرع للإغناء ، ألا يُرى أنها شرعت ساترةً، أو زاجرة، لا أمراً أصلياً للفقير إغناء له. وألا يُرى أنه تتأدى بالتحرير ،وبالصوم ولا إغناء فيهما، لكن المقصود به نيل الثواب ؛ ليقابل بموجب الجناية. وما تقع به كفاية الفقير في باب الكفارة يصلح سبباً للثواب، ولذلك تتأدى بالإباحة، ولا إغناء يحصل بها. فإذا لم يكن الإغناء مقصوداً: لم تُشترط صفة الغنى في المخاطب بها، بل القدرة واليُسر بها شرط، وذلك لا ينعدم بالدين، ويتبين أنها لم تجب شكراً للغنى، بل جزاءً للفعل، فلم يُشترط كمال صفة الغنى، وإنما شرط أدنى ما يصلح لكسب الثواب، وأصل المال كاف لذلك. وعلى هذا الأصل : يُخرَّج سقوط العُشر بهلاك الخارج؛ لأنه وجب بشرط القدرة الميسرة ؛ لأن القدرة على أداء العُشر تستغني عن قيام تسعة الأعشار ، لكنه شُرط ذلك ؛ لليسر، ولم يجب إلا بأرض نامية بالخارج، فشرط قيامه لبقاء صفة اليُسر. وكذلك الخراج يسقط إذا اصطلم الزرعَ آفة؛ لأنه إنما وجب بصفة اليُسر. ألا يُرى أنه لا يجب إلا بسلامة الخارج، إلا أنه بطريق التقدير بالتمكن ؛ لكون الواجب من غير جنس الخارج وبدليل أن الخارج إذا قل: حُطّ الخراجُ إلى نصف الخارج، ولما كان كذلك: سقط بهلاك الخارج، حتى لا ينقلب غُرماً محضاً.
And some said: Rather, it is obligatory with property and fasting does not suffice for it, unlike zakah. The difference is that zakah became obligatory with the attribute of ease, and the condition of ability, and for the meaning of enrichment by the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Make them independent of begging on such a day.' And by his saying (peace be upon him): 'There is no charity except from surplus wealth.' And this enrichment became obligatory as worship; gratitude for the blessing of wealth, so perfection was stipulated in its cause so that its gratitude may be deserved, so the obligatory is a portion of the perfect, and debt cancels perfection but does not eliminate its origin. Therefore charity became permissible for him, so enrichment is not obligatory upon him. Therefore zakah is only fulfilled with a specific valuable thing. Hadith: 'Make them independent of begging on such a day' narrated by Muhammad in al-Asl... Hadith: 'There is no charity except from surplus wealth' narrated by Imam Ahmad... As for expiation (kaffarah), it cannot dispense with the condition of ability and the existence of the attribute of ease in that ability, but it was not legislated for enrichment. Do you not see that it was legislated as a cover or a deterrent, not as an original matter for enriching the poor. Do you not see that it is fulfilled by freeing a slave and by fasting, and there is no enrichment in them, but the intent is to obtain reward, to counterbalance the consequence of the offense. And whatever suffices the poor in the chapter of expiation is suitable as a cause for reward, and therefore it is fulfilled by permission (ibaha), and no enrichment is obtained by it. So when enrichment is not intended, the attribute of wealth in the one addressed is not stipulated, but ability and ease in it are conditions, and that is not negated by debt, and it becomes clear that it was not obligatory as gratitude for wealth, but as a compensation for the act, so perfection of the attribute of wealth was not stipulated; rather, the minimum that is suitable for earning reward is stipulated, and the origin of property is sufficient for that. And upon this principle is derived the cancellation of 'ushr (tithe) upon destruction of the produce; because it was obligatory with the condition of easy ability; because the ability to pay 'ushr does not require the existence of nine-tenths, but that was stipulated for ease, and it was only obligatory due to land growing produce, so its existence was stipulated for the continuation of the attribute of ease. Similarly, kharaj (land tax) is cancelled if a blight destroys the crop; because it was only obligatory with the attribute of ease. Do you not see that it is only obligatory upon the safety of the produce, but it is by way of estimation based on capability; because the obligatory is not of the same type as the produce, and by evidence that if the produce is little, the kharaj is reduced to half of the produce. And since it is so, it is cancelled upon destruction of the produce, so that it does not turn into pure liability.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a detailed istinbat (derivation) from the Hanafi usul tradition, comparing the conditions of wealth (yusr) for different obligations: zakah (including sadaqat al-fitr), kaffarah (expiation), and land taxes ('ushr and kharaj). The author begins by addressing a dispute: some hold that sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory with property and cannot be fulfilled by fasting, unlike zakah. The Hanafi response explains that zakah is founded on the attribute of ease (yusr) and the condition of ability (qudra), and its purpose is enrichment (ighna') as per the hadith 'Make them independent of begging on this day' and 'No charity except from surplus wealth.' This enrichment is an act of worship and gratitude, requiring perfection in its cause (surplus wealth). Debt removes that perfection but not the origin, so a person with debt may still take sadaqah but is not obliged to give it, and zakah is only fulfilled with a specific valuable asset. Next, the author contrasts kaffarah: it too requires ability and ease, but is not legislated for enrichment. Rather, it is a covering or deterrent, fulfilled by freeing a slave or fasting—actions that do not enrich anyone. The aim is reward to counterbalance sin. Therefore, the condition of wealth is not full perfection; only minimal ability to earn reward suffices, and debt does not negate that. The author then extends this principle to 'ushr and kharaj: 'ushr is cancelled if produce is destroyed because it was obliged with a condition of easy ability—the existence of the produce for ease, not for the payer's wealth. Similarly, kharaj is cancelled by blight because it depends on the existence of produce; if produce is minimal, tax is reduced, and if destroyed, it is cancelled to avoid becoming pure liability. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of talil (reasoning) and qiyas based on the underlying purpose (ighna' vs. non-ighna') of each obligation.

Key Terms
الإغناء (al-ighnā’): Making the poor independent of begging; the purpose of sadaqat al-fitr and zakah, requiring the giver to have surplus wealth.
اليُسر (al-yusr): Ease or ability; a condition for obligations like zakah, kaffarah, 'ushr, and kharaj, but its degree varies.
الدين (al-dayn): Debt; it cancels the perfection (kamal) of wealth but not its origin (asl), so it affects obligations differently.
القدرة الميسرة (al-qudra al-muyassara): Easy ability; a condition for 'ushr and kharaj, meaning the produce itself must exist for the obligation to stand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle in this passage, why does kaffarah not require the condition of 'ighna' (enrichment) unlike zakah?
A) Because kaffarah is a punishment and must be difficult.
B) Because kaffarah is legislated as a cover (satira) or deterrent (zajira), not to enrich the poor.
C) Because kaffarah can only be fulfilled by fasting, which inherently involves poverty.
D) Because the poor are not mentioned in the verses of kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
The condition of wealth varies by obligation: full surplus for enrichment-based duties, minimal ability for expiation, and produce-existence for land taxes.

Intention in Fasting: Specific vs. Absolute
Hanafi vs. Shafi'i dispute on necessity of specifying intention for Ramadan fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Hanafi vs. Shafi'i dispute on specification of intention for Ramadan fasting, applying the usul principle that an act uniquely determined by its time does not require additional specification.

Core Idea
When the law prescribes only one act in a given time, an absolute intention suffices to fulfill it.

This passage presents a key usul dispute on whether intention must specify the act (e.g., fasting for Ramadan) when the time is uniquely dedicated to that act. The Hanafi school argues that because Ramadan has no other prescribed fast, an absolute intention to fast automatically counts for Ramadan. The Shafi'i school insists on explicit specification to ensure conscious devotion. We'll trace the arguments and the Hanafi rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the core issue: is specification of intention (ta'ayyun al-niyyah) necessary for Ramadan fasting according to the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools?
2
State Hanafi position and proof
Explain that for a traveler or sick person, an absolute intention suffices because the time is uniquely for Ramadan. Note the analogy with zakat after the year: giving a gift to a poor automatically counts as zakat.
The Hanafi dalil is based on the uniqueness of the time and the non-existence of any other prescribed fast in Ramadan.
3
State Shafi'i position and proof
Explain that Imam al-Shafi'i requires specification because the servant's benefits remain his property; without specification, he would be compelled and devotion is negated.
4
Analyze Hanafi response
Show how the Hanafi rebuts: when the prescribed act is one in that time, it is determined by time itself; absolute intention acts as specification. Also distinguish advance specification (valid) from intervening specification (invalid).
Key distinction: the fast is indivisible, so missing intention at the start invalidates the whole for Shafi'i; but Hanafi says since the time is unique, initial resolve applies to the whole.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a traveler who fasts without specifying Ramadan has fulfilled his obligation according to Hanafi; Shafi'i requires him to redo with specific intention.

وفيه روايتان عنه. وأما إذا أطلق النية : فالصحيح أن يقع عن رمضان؛ لأن الترخص والترك لا يتحقق بهذه العزيمة. وأما المريض: فإن الصحيح عندنا فيه : أن يقع صومه بكل حال عن 6 رمضان؛ لأن رخصته متعلقة بحقيقة العجز فيظهر بنفس الصوم فواتُ شرط الرخصة، فيلحق بالصحيح. وأما المسافر: فيستوجب الرخصة بعجز مقدر بقيام سببه، وهو السفر، فلا يظهر بنفس الصوم فوات شرط الرخصة ، فلا يبطل الترخص. فيتعدى حينئذ بطريق التنبيه الحول، وكأجير الواحد يستحق منافعه. قلنا : ليس التعيين باستحقاق لمنافع العبد ؛ لأن ذلك لا يصلح قُربة، وإنما القُربة فعل يفعله العبد عن اختيار بلا جبر، بل الشرع لم يشرع في هذا الوقت مما يتصور فيه الإمساك قُربةً إلا واحداً، فانعدم غير الفرض الوقتي ؛ لعدم كونه مشروعاً، لا باستحقاق منافعه، كما ينعدم في الليل أصلاً، ولا استحقاق ثمةَ ، فإذا بقيت المنافع له : لم يكن بد من التعيين ولم يوجد ؛ لأن عدم العزيمة ليس بشيءٍ، بخلاف هبة النصاب؛ لأنه عبادة تصلح مجازاً الصدقة ؛ استحسانا . عن وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : لما كانت منافعه بقيت على ملكه وجب التعيين حتى يصير مختاراً، لا مجبوراً ، ولو وضعنا عنه تعيين الجهة : لصار مجبوراً في صفة العبادة، ولخلا معنى العبادة عن الإقبال والعزيمة. وقلنا الأمر على ما قلت إلا أنه لما اتحد المشروع في هذا الوقت: تعين في زمانه، فأصيب بمطلق الاسم ، ولم يُفقد بالخطأ في الوصف، كالمتعين في مكانه فصار جوازه بهذه النية على أنه تعيين، لا على أن التعيين عنه موضوع، فكان هذا منا قولاً بموجب العلة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : لما وجب التعيين شرطاً بالإجماع: وجب من أوله ؛ لأن أول أجزائه فعل مفتقر إلى العزيمة، فإذا تراخى بطل، فإذا اعترضت العزيمة من بعد: لم تُؤثر في الماضي بوجه؛ لأن إخلاص العبد فيما قد عمله لا يتحقق، وإنما هو لما لم يعمله بعد، فإذا فسد ذلك الجزء: فسد الباقي ؛ لأنه لا يتجزأ، ووجب ترجيح جانب الفساد ؛ احتياطاً. وهذا بخلاف التقديم ؛ لأن التقديم واقع على جملة الإمساك، ولم يعترض عليه ما يُبطله فبقي وأما المعترض فلا يحتمل التقديم. ألا يُرى أن النية بعد نصف النهار It is prescribed, so its performance is valid. And because performance is not required from him during his travel, this time in terms of fulfilling what is upon him became like Sha'ban, so it accepts the rest of the fasts. The first way necessitates that the voluntary fast is not valid but rather occurs as the obligatory one. The second way necessitates that it is valid, and there are two transmissions from him about it. As for when he releases the intention, the correct view is that it occurs for Ramadan, because concession and abandonment are not realized with this resolve. As for the sick person, the correct view with us is that his fast occurs in any case for Ramadan, because his concession is connected to the reality of incapacity, so the vanishing of the condition of the concession becomes apparent by the fast itself, thus he joins the healthy person. As for the traveler, he becomes entitled to the concession by an estimated incapacity due to the existence of its cause, which is travel. So the vanishing of the condition of the concession does not become apparent by the fast itself, so the concession is not invalidated. Then it extends by way of indication to his religious need. Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Since the time became specifically determined for this prescribed act, what can be conceived of abstaining in this time becomes due from the doer, so it occurs for the one entitled in any case, like the owner of the nisab when he gives it as a gift to the poor after the year, and like the single hireling whose benefits are owed. We said: The determination is not because the benefits of the servant are owed, for that is not valid as a devotional act. Rather, the devotional act is an action that the servant does by choice without compulsion. Rather, the Law has not prescribed in this time, among what can be conceived of abstaining, any devotional act except one. So the other than the timed obligatory act is non-existent due to its being unprescribed, not due to the owing of his benefits, just as it is non-existent at night completely, and there is no owing there. So when the benefits remain his, there must be specification and it did not occur, because the absence of resolve is nothing. Unlike the gift of the nisab, because it is a devotional act that is metaphorically valid as charity by istihsan. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Since his benefits remained his property, specification became necessary so that he becomes a chooser, not compelled. If we removed from him the specification of the direction, he would become compelled in the quality of the worship, and the meaning of worship would be devoid of devotion and resolve. We said: The matter is as you said, except that when the prescribed act is one in this time, it becomes specifically determined in its time, so it is hit by the absolute name, and is not lost by error in the description, like that which is specifically determined in its place. So its permissibility with this intention is as specification, not that specification is dropped from him. So this from us is a statement in accordance with the cause. And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Since specification is required as a condition by consensus, it is required from the beginning, because the first of its parts is an action needing resolve. If it delays, it becomes invalid. If resolve occurs later, it does not affect the past in any way, because the sincerity of the servant in what he has already done cannot be realized; it is only for what he has not yet done. So when that part is corrupted, the rest is corrupted because it is indivisible, and it is necessary to give preponderance to the side of corruption as a precaution. This is unlike advance specification, because advance specification occurs upon the whole period of abstaining, and nothing occurs to invalidate it, so it remains. But the intervening specification does not tolerate advance. Do you not see that the intention after midday is not valid? Do you not see that in the fast of debt, it is necessary to distinguish between these two aspects?
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i on the necessity of specifying the intention (ta'ayyun al-niyyah) for fasting in Ramadan. The issue arises when a person in a situation of concession (rukhsa) — such as a traveler or sick person — fasts without expressly intending Ramadan. The Hanafi position, attributed to Abu Hanifa, is that because Ramadan is uniquely determined by its time, an absolute intention to fast suffices; the fast automatically falls for Ramadan. The passage first discusses the traveler: since performance is not required from him during travel, the time becomes like Sha'ban (where voluntary fasts are permissible), so his fast is accepted. If he absolutely intends, it counts for Ramadan because the concession does not negate the resolve. For the sick person, the concession is based on actual incapacity, so his fasting shows the condition for the concession is absent, thus he joins the healthy. For the traveler, the concession is based on an estimated incapacity (cause: travel), so fasting does not negate the concession. Zufar argues that since the time is uniquely determined for this prescribed act, the abstaining becomes due from the doer and falls for the one entitled (i.e., Ramadan), analogous to a zakat owner giving his nisab to a poor person after the year — it counts as zakat automatically. The Hanafi response (qulna) refines: the determination is not because the servant's benefits are owed (they are not owned by Allah like a hireling), but because the Law has not prescribed any other fast in this time except the obligatory one. Therefore, only one act exists, so the absolute intention specifies it. The Shafi'i argument: since the benefits remain the servant's property, he must specify the intention to be a chooser, not compelled; otherwise, the worship lacks devotion and resolve. The Hanafi rejoinder: when the prescribed act is one in that time, it becomes specifically determined by the time itself, so the absolute name suffices, like something determined by its place. The second Shafi'i argument: specification is required from the beginning because intention at the start is necessary; if it is missing, the first part is invalid, and since the fast is indivisible, the whole is void. The Hanafi distinction: advance specification (like intending for Ramadan the night before) is valid, but intervening specification (like intending during the day) is not, as seen in the rule that intention after midday is invalid for Ramadan. The passage ends by noting a distinction for a make-up fast (qada). This debate illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that when an act is uniquely identified by its time or cause, no additional specification in intention is required.

Key Terms
التعيين (al-ta'ayyun): Specification of the act in intention (e.g., intending specifically for Ramadan rather than a general fast).
الرخصة (al-rukhsa): A concession granted by the Law that allows deviation from the original ruling due to a valid excuse (e.g., travel, illness).
العزيمة (al-'azima): Resolve or firm intention in performance of an act, indicating conscious choice and devotion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, if a traveler fasts in Ramadan without specifying whether it is for Ramadan or something else, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is invalid and must be repeated with a specific intention.
B) The fast counts for Ramadan because the time is uniquely determined for Ramadan, and an absolute intention suffices.
C) The fast counts as a voluntary fast only.
D) The fast is suspended until the traveler specifies his intention later.

Key Takeaway
When a time is uniquely dedicated to one prescribed act, an absolute intention to perform that category of act is automatically specified to that act, even without verbal or mental specification.

The Necessity of Intention for Continuous Acts of Worship
Explaining the necessity of intention for continuous acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul reasoning that fasting is an indivisible continuous act requiring intention at its beginning, and apply the analogy with prayer to similar acts.

Core Idea
Fasting is one continuous indivisible act; intention must cover its beginning, not its continuation.

This lesson explores the foundational usul principle behind the requirement of intention (niyyah) for fasting. The author argues that refraining (imsak) is a continuous act of worship that is indivisible—it is either valid or invalid as a whole. Because of this nature, intention is necessary at the start, analogous to the takbir in prayer. The analysis introduces key concepts like 'azima (resolution), rukhsah (concession), and virtual existence, which are crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to continuous acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its nature
Recognize that the author classifies imsak (refraining) as a single, continuous act of worship that cannot be partial in validity or invalidity.
This is the basis for requiring intention at the beginning.
2
Apply the analogy with prayer
Understand how the states of beginning and remaining in fasting are analogous to prayer: the initial takbir is essential, but continuation does not require constant renewal.
The author explicitly compares the two acts.
3
Explain the dropping of 'azima
Note that steadfastness on resolution ('azima) is dropped by consensus due to inability at the time of performance and at the start. This allows for virtual existence of intention.
This concession is central to the timing debate.
4
Distinguish virtual and actual existence
The author introduces the idea that intention may exist virtually (taqdīran) even if not actual, giving it the merit of comprehensiveness.
This is a key usul tool for justifying delayed intention.
5
Analyze the role of inability and preponderance
Consider how the inability to intend from the start (e.g., waking after dawn) leads to a concession, and how preponderance (tarjih) between existence and quality is resolved.
This sets the stage for the specific rulings on fard and nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقلنا نحن إن الحاجة إلى النية؛ لأن الإمساك قُربةً، وهذا يصير الإمساك واحدٌ غير متجزئ صحةً وفساداً، والثبات على العزيمة حالَ الأداء ساقط بالإجماع؛ للعجز، وحالَ الشروع في الأداء ابتداء ساقط بالإجماع أيضاً؛ للعجز ، وصار حال الابتداء ها هنا: نظير حال البقاء في الصلاة، وحالُ البقاء : نظير حال الابتداء في الصلاة.
ثم هذا العجز أطلق التقديم مع الفصل عن ركن العبادة، وجعل موجوداً تقديراً، فصار له فضل الاستيعاب، ونقصان حقيقة الوجود عند الأداء على حد الإخلاص، والعجز الداعي إلى التأخير موجود في الجملة في جنس من يقيم بعد الصبح، أو يفيق عن إغمائه.
وفي يوم الفرض حرامٌ ، ونيةُ النفل عندك لغو، فقد جاءت الضرورة، فلأن يثبت بها التأخير مع الوصل بالركن أولى ، ولهذا رجحان في الوجود عند الفعل وهو حد حقيقة الأصل، ونقصان القصور عن الجملة بقليل: يحتمل العفو، فاستويا في طريق الرخصة، بل هذا أرجح.
وهذا الوجه يوجب الكفارة بالفطر فيه، وروي ذلك عنهما، ولما صح الاقتصار على البعض للضرورة وجب المصير إلى ما له حكم الكل من الكل من كل وجه، وهو أن يُشترط الوجود في الأكثر ؛ لأن خَلَفاً وجه الأقل في مقابلة الأكثر : في حكم العدم، ولا ضرورة في ترك هذا الكل الثابت تقديراً، فلم نجوزه بعد الزوال، ورجحنا الكثير على القليل؛ لأنه في الوجود راجح ، وبطل الترجيح بصفة العبادة؛ لأنه حال بعد الوجود، والكثرة والقلة من باب الوجود، والوجود قبل الحال، فوجب الترجيح به، على ما يأتي بيانه في باب الترجيح إن شاء الله تعالى.
ولأن صيانة الوقت الذي لا دَرَك له أصلاً على العباد واجبة، وهو معنى قول مشايخنا رحمهم الله : إن أداء العبادة في وقتها أولى، فصار هذا الترجيح متعارضاً ، وهذا الوجه يوجب أن لا كفارة فيه، ويُروى ذلك عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه. ولم نقل بالاستناد ، ولا بفساد الجزء الأول مع احتمال طريق الصحة. والإمساك في أول النهار قُربةٌ مع قصور معنى الطاعة فيه؛ لأنه لا مشقة في الإمساك في أول النهار، فصار إثبات العزيمة فيه تقديراً، لا تحقيقاً؛ وفاء لحقه، وتوفيراً لحظه.
وعلى هذا الأصل قلنا : إن صوم النفل مقدر بكل اليوم، حتى فسد بوجود المنافي في أوله ولم يُتأدَّ إلا من أوله، ولم يتأدَّ بالنية في الآخر؛ لأن الصوم عُرف قُربةً بمعياره، ولم يُعرف معياره إلا بيوم كامل، فلم يجز شرع العبادة بالرأي.
وأما الإمساك في أول يوم النحر، فلم يُشرع صوماً، ولكن ليكون ابتداء التناول من القرابين؛ كراهيةً للأضياف أن يتناولوا من غير طعام الضيافة قبل طعامها.
ومن هذا الجنس الصوم المنذور في وقت بعينه : لما انقلب بالنذر صوم الوقت واجباً لم يبق نفلاً ؛ لأنه واحدٌ لا يقبل وصفين متضادين، فصار واحداً من هذا الوجه، فأصيب بمطلق الاسم.
We said that there is a need for intention because refraining (imsak) is an act of worship, and this makes refraining one indivisible thing in validity and invalidity. Steadfastness upon resolution ('azima) at the time of performance is dropped by consensus due to inability, and at the beginning of performance is also dropped by consensus due to inability. So the state of beginning here is analogous to the state of remaining in prayer, and the state of remaining is analogous to the state of beginning in prayer. Then this inability allowed advancement with separation from the pillar of worship, and it is considered existing virtually. So it gets the merit of comprehensiveness, but deficiency in actual existence at performance is on the level of sincerity. The inability that calls for delay exists in general in the category of one who rises after dawn or regains consciousness from a faint. And on the day of an obligatory (fast), it is forbidden, and the intention of voluntary (fast) according to you is futile. Necessity has come, so to establish delay with connection to the pillar is more appropriate. And for this, there is preponderance in existence at the act, which is the limit of the reality of the principle. And the deficiency of shortcoming from the entirety by a little is liable to pardon. So they become equal in the path of concession; rather this is more preponderant. This aspect necessitates expiation for breaking the fast in it, and that was narrated from the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And when restricting to some is valid due to necessity, it is necessary to resort to what has the ruling of the whole from the whole in every respect, which is that existence is required in the majority, because the aspect of the minority in comparison to the majority is in the ruling of non-existence. There is no necessity to leave this whole that is virtually established, so we did not permit it after noon, and we gave preponderance to the many over the few because it is preponderant in existence. And the preponderance is invalidated by the quality of worship because it is a state after existence, and quantity and quality are from the category of existence, and existence is prior to the state, so preponderance must be given to it, as will be explained in the chapter on preponderance, God willing. And because safeguarding the time that has no substitute is obligatory upon servants, and that is the meaning of our scholars' saying: 'Performing worship in its time is superior.' So this preponderance becomes conflicting. This aspect necessitates that there be no expiation in it, and that was narrated from Abu Hanifa, may God be pleased with him. We did not say by reliance (istinad) nor by invalidity of the first part with the possibility of the path of validity. And refraining in the beginning of the day is an act of worship despite the deficiency of the meaning of obedience in it because there is no hardship in refraining at the beginning of the day. So establishing the resolution in it is virtual, not actual; fulfilling its right and increasing its share. Upon this principle we said: The voluntary fast is defined by the entire day, such that it becomes invalid by the existence of a contradictory in its beginning, and it is not performed except from its beginning, and it is not performed by intention in the latter part because fasting is known as worship by its standard, and its standard is not known except by a complete day, so it is not permissible to legislate worship by opinion. As for refraining at the beginning of the Day of Sacrifice, it was not legislated as a fast, but rather so that the beginning of consumption from the sacrificial animals be out of dislike for the guests to eat from other than the food of hospitality before its food. And from this category is the vowed fast in a specific time: when the fast of that time becomes obligatory due to the vow, it does not remain voluntary, because it is one thing that does not accept two contradictory attributes, so it becomes one from this aspect, and it is affected by the absolute name.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul analysis of the necessity and timing of intention (niyyah) for fasting. The author explains that refraining from eating (imsak) is a continuous act of worship that is indivisible—it is either valid or invalid as a whole. The strict resolution ('azima) to fast is required at the beginning but is dropped due to inability (e.g., for someone who does not intend from night). This parallels prayer where the initial takbir is essential but the continuation is not. The text then differentiates between obligatory (fard) and voluntary (nafl) fasts. For a fard fast, intending from the night is generally required, but necessity can permit delay. For nafl, the intention must be for the entire day; breaking it early invalidates the fast. On the Day of Sacrifice, refraining at dawn is not a fast but merely a recommended delay to share the feast. Vowed fasts become obligatory, thus follow the rules of fard. The passage also discusses conflicting rulings on expiation, narrating differences between Abu Hanifa and his two companions. The key usul principles applied are: the necessity of intention for continuous acts, the distinction between virtual and actual existence, and preponderance (tarjih) between conflicting evidences.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; the resolve to perform an act of worship for the sake of Allah, necessary for distinguishing acts of worship from habits.
عزيمة ('azima): Resolution; the original strict ruling that is not abrogated or relaxed.
إمساك (imsak): Refraining from eating, drinking, and marital relations during the fasting period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason given in the passage for the necessity of intention at the beginning of a fast?
A) Because refraining is a single indivisible act of worship.
B) Because it is a consensus of the companions.
C) Because it is clear from the Quran.
D) Because it is a condition from the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Fasting is a continuous indivisible act requiring intention at its start; the analogy with prayer and the concept of virtual existence justify delayed intention due to necessity.

Timing of Intention for Fard, Nafl, and Nadhr Fasts
Explaining timing of intention for different fast types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on intention timing for fard, nafl, and vowed fasts, and evaluate the internal dispute on expiation when intention is delayed.

Core Idea
For obligatory fasts, intention may be delayed due to necessity; for voluntary fasts, the entire day must be intended from the start.

This lesson delves into the specific applications of the usul principle established earlier. The passage distinguishes between obligatory (fard) and voluntary (nafl) fasts regarding the timing of intention. For a fard fast, necessity (like waking after dawn) permits delaying intention until noon. For a nafl fast, intention must cover the whole day; if a nullifier occurs at the start, the fast is invalid. The passage also discusses vowed fasts and the special case of the Day of Sacrifice. Additionally, an internal Hanafi dispute on expiation for breaking a fast with delayed intention is examined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of fasts
Distinguish fard (obligatory), nafl (voluntary), and nadhr (vowed) fasts in the passage.
Each has different rules for intention timing.
2
Apply the necessity concession to fard fasts
Understand that for fard, the inability to intend from the night allows delay until noon, as per the principle of virtual existence.
The text says 'وفي يوم الفرض حرامٌ' and then allows delay.
3
Analyze the ruling for nafl fasts
The passage states that nfl fasts are measured by the whole day; if a nullifier occurs at the beginning, the fast is invalid. Intention cannot be made in the latter part.
This is because the standard of the worship is a full day.
4
Apply the same to vowed fasts
A vowed fast becomes obligatory like fard, so it follows the same rules; it does not remain voluntary.
The text says 'لم يبق نفلاً' because it cannot have two contradictory attributes.
5
Examine the expiation dispute
Two conflicting narrations: from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad requiring expiation, from Abu Hanifa not requiring expiation. The passage presents both without final tarjih.
This shows the internal ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul analysis of the necessity and timing of intention (niyyah) for fasting. The author explains that refraining from eating (imsak) is a continuous act of worship that is indivisible—it is either valid or invalid as a whole. Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; the resolve to perform an act of worship.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation; a penalty for breaking a fast without valid reason, usually fasting for two months or feeding the poor.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary act of worship; supererogatory.
واجب (wajib): Obligatory; binding duty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is the ruling on a voluntary fast if a nullifier occurs at the very beginning of the day?
A) The fast is valid because intention covers the whole day.
B) The fast becomes invalid and must be made up.
C) The fast is valid but the person must avoid nullifiers for the rest of the day.
D) The fast is invalid and expiation is required.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory fasts allow delayed intention until noon due to necessity; voluntary fasts require intention from dawn; vowed fasts follow obligatory rules.
